Yesterday Evening Reception for Postal Staff by the Press

Reasons for Opposing the Establishment of a Separate Bureau for Postal Savings and Remittances

Report on the Resolution of Ten Outstanding Issues

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union and the Postal Employees' Union hosted a banquet for reporters from various newspapers at the Central Western Restaurant yesterday. Dozens of reporters from various newspapers attended. During the banquet, representatives from both unions reported on the reasons for opposing the establishment of a separate bureau for postal savings and remittances, as well as the various acts of greed, corruption, and destruction of the postal system by Liu Shufan, the Director of the Postal Department of the Ministry of Communications and concurrently the Director-General of the Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau.

They stated that the postal savings and remittance business has always been handled by the post office. Since Liu Shufan went abroad for inspection last year and returned to China in August, he has gained nothing but arranged for a large number of private individuals to be placed in positions, and at the expense of dividing the postal service, he has established a separate bureau to handle the savings and remittance business. Since the establishment of this redundant agency, the postal budget has increased by six million yuan. The facts of his disrupting the postal organization, disturbing the governance, and destroying the regulations are truly heartbreaking to speak of.

The biggest reason for Liu's desire to establish a separate bureau for the savings and remittance business is nothing more than imitating the practices of various countries, saying that European countries all manage postal savings and remittance affairs separately from other postal matters, and Japan also adopted this system early on. In fact, the postal organization systems of various countries are completely different from what Liu said. Those of us who know a little about the current postal situation in Britain, the United States, and Japan all believe that Liu's statement is unfounded. The documents submitted by the two unions to the Central Party Headquarters and various ministries and departments detail the postal situation in various countries.

The purpose of savings and remittances is to promote thrift, not to be similar to private commercial banks, and since the establishment of the Savings and Remittances Bureau, the so-called new policies it boasts of are all similar to what ordinary banks have already done well, and as a result, it has only led to a decline in business. Moreover, the bureau's external credit is guaranteed by the post office. Since the post office is already providing the guarantee, it can be handled by the post office. Why is it necessary to establish a separate bureau, wasting huge sums of money, seemingly separating but not separating, and what is the intention? It is self-evident. In short, based on all the facts, the savings and remittance business cannot be developed and the public's trust cannot be strengthened unless it is merged with the post office. This is a brief reason why the Savings and Remittances Bureau should be merged with the post office.

As for Liu Shufan's crimes of greed, corruption, and destruction of the postal system, let's cite a few of the most obvious ones: (1) Destroying the Postal Association, which planned to recover postal rights in the first year of the Republic of China; (2) Repeated speculation during the Longtan battle the year before last; (3) Causing labor unrest in the seventeenth year, instigating the police to strip the mail carriers of their national uniforms, and sowing discord to undermine the two unions; (4) Not uttering a word at the International Postal Union meeting in London last year, losing national dignity and returning; (5) Taking advantage of his promotion to Director-General to dismiss himself, using fraudulent means to embezzle 120,000 yuan of public funds; (6) Spending tens of thousands of yuan of public funds on repairs to his private residence; (7) Destroying the postal examination system, appointing private individuals who have not passed the old examination, and turning the Savings and Remittances Bureau into his personal enterprise, with all personnel being either relatives of Liu or fathers, sons, brothers, uncles, and nephews; (8) Other acts such as controlling the postal service, destroying the postal system, forming factions for personal gain, and excluding dissidents are too numerous to mention. In short, Liu's lifelong behavior has been greedy and despicable. His past history has been nothing more than flattering foreigners to gain merit. Recent facts show that petty people are triumphant, wielding great power alone to create a postal system for one family and one faction, in order to achieve his conspiracy to control the postal service.

The two unions have submitted documents to the Central Party Headquarters and various ministries and departments, appealing for fair handling, and it is heard that the Central Political Conference has handed it over to the Economic Group for review. Furthermore, the ten demands of the two unions were resolved last month. These demands are all extremely legitimate and are not unreasonable demands or ulterior motives. The smooth resolution and the understanding of the staff and workers of the difficulties of the authorities can be seen as true, they said.

In addition, the Shanghai Postal Workers' Union and the Shanghai Postal Employees' Union submitted another document to the Legislative Yuan and the Executive Yuan regarding the abolition of the Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau, stating that the establishment of the Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau was inappropriate based on the systems of various countries and the current methods, and there is no reason for its existence.

The staff and unions have already submitted a case against the separate establishment of the Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau. However, there are still some things that have not been fully stated in the previous submission, so we dare to reiterate them below.

It is found that the current Director of the Postal Department, Liu Shufan, went abroad for inspection for eight months and gained nothing, but arranged for a large number of private individuals to be placed in positions, and at the expense of suggesting the establishment of this redundant agency, and the biggest reason for it is nothing more than (imitating the practices of various countries), so there are statements such as (European countries all manage postal savings and remittance affairs separately from other postal matters, and Japan also adopted this system early on). However, it is known that the postal organization systems of various countries are completely different from what Liu said. According to the latest promulgated postal regulations of various countries and the current postal organization status of various countries printed by the London International Postal Union, there is no such thing. Let's take the current situation in Britain, the United States, and Japan as an example. The British postal service was established the earliest, and the United States and Japan have imitated it in many ways. Other countries need not be mentioned. The British Postmaster General is in charge of everything, and there are various secretaries under him, each managing the affairs under his jurisdiction, such as postal lotus telegrams, remittances, personnel, etc., each is handled separately, and there is also an Accountant General who is in charge of finance and implements the spirit of accounting independence, and all financial and economic accounting matters are under his full authority. As for postal savings, it is only one of the matters he handles.

Under the Postmaster General of the United States, there are four Assistant Postmaster Generals, and under each Assistant Postmaster General, there are various divisions, and the Savings Division and the Remittance Division, together with the Finance Division, the Stamp Division, and the Registered Mail Division, are all under the third Assistant Postmaster General. As for the Japanese postal system, it is all imitated from Britain and the United States and there is nothing special. The Japanese Ministry of Communications (also known as Postmaster General in English) has various bureaus under it, but although their names are bureaus, they are actually no different from the departments of Britain and the United States. From the above, it can be seen that the two items of savings and remittances are both subordinate to the Postmaster General. The so-called separate management refers to separate offices and divisions for special management. This system was originally the case in our country. Moreover, the savings and remittance business in Britain, the United States, and Japan is developed, which cannot be compared with our country, and there is no separate bureau and large-scale extravagance. Liu Shufan erased the facts and fabricated words to deceive, which not only confused the postal service but also made friendly countries laugh. Some people say that the position of the Postmaster General in Britain and the United States is almost equal to the position of the Minister of Communications in our country, so the Postmaster General of our country and the Director-General of Savings and Remittances may as well be under the Minister of Communications.

Page 14

In fact, this is a big mistake. It must be known that although the position of the Postmaster General in Britain, the United States, and Japan is raised as much as possible and is equal to a cabinet member, there is no special official in charge of postal affairs under the Postmaster General, and the part that manages the savings and remittance business, no matter how developed its business is, is ultimately subordinate to the Postmaster General and cannot be on par with the Postmaster General. This is another fact that proves that Liu Shufan's absurd remarks are self-defeating. This is also a reason why, based on the systems of various countries, the savings and remittance business should still be handled by the post office.

Furthermore, the purpose of postal savings and remittances in various countries is to promote thrift and facilitate the people, especially to restrict people's savings in the post office reserves as much as possible. Let's cite a passage from Chapter 6 of the British Postal Regulations: The purpose of the national establishment of postal savings is to set up a savings institution to promote thrift, not to collect current deposits. If an account is opened for a minor, or the purpose of opening the account is different from the original intention of establishing postal savings, the Accountant General has the right to cancel it.) It is true that the needs and purposes of postal savings and remittances are completely different from those of national banks. If it is to increase deposits, and no effort is spared to attract customers, wouldn't there be a conflict with the country's central bank? The main reason why Liu Shufan suggested the establishment of the Savings and Remittances Bureau is that the savings and remittances handled by the post office were not developed before, and it is necessary to establish a separate bureau. According to the domestic national conditions and foreign precedents, it is exactly the opposite. Let's divide the two into two parts. One is what other countries do not have, but we brazenly implement it. The purpose of postal savings and remittances is to promote thrift and facilitate the people. The policies adopted are different from those of the national central bank and even more unlike private commercial banks. The so-called new policies of the Savings and Remittances Bureau are to increase current deposits (using checks) and fixed deposits (more than several years), which is contrary to the principles of postal savings.

The second is what other countries have, but we cannot implement. Liu Shufan boasts that the clearing item has not yet been held, so it is added as one of the new policies. In fact, if we examine our country's commercial habits, each store settles accounts only at the end of the year, which is not as good as foreign merchants who implement clearing. If you want the clearing to be developed, this time is not yet right in China. Even in major trading ports, various banks have already done it better. Moreover, according to the actual operation of the postal savings business, it is absolutely different from ordinary banks. Most of the money received by ordinary banks is invested locally, which can avoid the depreciation of clearing, while the money from postal savings must be remitted to the special bureau. For example, in Guangdong Province postal savings, there are many local deposits, but there are no investment opportunities locally. If you remit money out, the remittance rate is surprisingly high, so the interest rate is reduced to 3.6% (the rest are 4.5%). However, it is still considered too much, so new accounts are closed. This refers to Guangdong double silver coins. The currency system is not unified in various places, so the silver prices are different in various places, and the root cause of the underdeveloped savings and remittance business lies in this. It is not only gratifying to increase the number of deposits. This is the second reason why the purpose is wrong.

Furthermore, the annual budget expenditure of the Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau must be as high as 6 million yuan. If the income from deposits is invested to generate profits, in addition to paying interest to depositors, if each yuan can get a net profit of 3%, there must be at least 200 million yuan in deposits to make up for this huge amount of expenditure. However, the actual deposits, the total amount in the country, is only 10 million yuan. Moreover, it is very important to note that the 6 million yuan in the bureau's budget only refers to all the expenses of the bureau, while the salaries and other expenses of the postal staff in various bureaus across the country who handle the savings and remittance business are not included. If it is actually calculated, it must be more than doubled, which will exceed 400 million yuan. Considering the domestic economic situation, with years of war, floods, and droughts, such a huge amount of deposits is definitely impossible and need not be discussed. The Shanghai banks are extremely frugal in their expenses. For example, the Jin Cheng Bank only spends 2,000 yuan per month excluding rent, while the Savings and Remittances Bureau leases office buildings from the accumulated surplus company, which is still contracted by the post office, with hundreds of taels per month. Other section chiefs and other staff are numerous and the expenses are huge. If it is merged into the post office, this 6 million expenditure can be saved. This is the third reason why the savings and remittances should be merged into the post office in terms of huge expenditure.

Furthermore, the bureau's current external credit has become a bank with no capital, because the post office handles savings and remittances, and the postal assets and other income of the post office serve as collateral, so the credit is strong, while the Savings and Remittances Bureau has no assets and only uses the post office as collateral, and also includes the budget settlement into the postal budget settlement. Since it is clear that it is attached to the post office, it can be directly merged into the post office. Wouldn't it be straightforward, and it must be seemingly separate but not separate, and the intention is already unpredictable. This is the fourth reason why the savings and remittance business should be merged into the post office in terms of external credit.

To sum up the above four points, these are all the reasons why the postal savings and remittance business should not be established as a separate bureau, and the reasons why it cannot be established as a separate bureau. It is reasonable to continue to prepare a document and submit it to your office for review, and to quickly reject the bureau's regulations, which is really for public convenience. Sincerely presented,

Liu Shufan Submitted His Resignation Yesterday

Requesting to be Dismissed from All Concurrent Positions

Liu Shufan, Director of the Postal Department of the Ministry of Communications and concurrently Director-General of the Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau, submitted his resignation to the Ministry of Communications because of misunderstandings and criticisms from the outside world. The original text of his resignation, which was submitted yesterday, is as follows:

Submitting this document to express my sincerity and request that you forward it to request dismissal from all my concurrent positions. I, Shufan, was summoned to Beijing in the sixteenth year of the Republic of China while serving as the Postal Director of Anhui to reorganize postal affairs. At that time, military affairs were flourishing, the political situation was precarious, and labor unrest was surging. The postal service, which had a complete system, was also facing a crisis and was in danger of being destroyed. I, Shufan, obeyed the instructions of the superiors and worked diligently for the public, with the original intention of cherishing the post office and maintaining the general work in a dangerous situation. Relying on your virtue and power, it was fortunate that postal transportation and military transportation to the front lines were not affected before the Northern Expedition was completed. However, at that time, Beiping had not yet fallen, and all postal power and its entire economy, as well as postal ticket files, etc., were still under the control of the foreign Director-General of the Northern Bureau. Although the negotiations had been agreed upon, the implementation was still difficult. It was not until the recovery of Pingjin and the completion of unification that the power of the foreigners who had controlled the postal service for decades was completely recovered and returned to the control of our government. Then, plans were made in advance, such as streamlining redundant personnel, saving waste, improving treatment, and expanding postal services. These major points were gradually implemented, all relying on your long-term plans to achieve good results. In March of the eighteenth year, I, Shufan, was ordered to attend the International Postal Conference and inspect postal affairs in various countries. I originally intended to complete the mission and retreat to the path of virtuousness to relieve the burden. However, after returning to the country, I tried to resign but was unable to do so and returned to my original position as Director of the Postal Department. Therefore, based on what I learned from the inspection, I selected the most effective and practical matters that are most needed and useful for our country, such as savings and remittance matters, and reported them to the superiors. I was honored to be adopted and was immediately commissioned to plan the establishment of a special bureau for savings and remittances in accordance with the practices of various countries to benefit the people's livelihood. I immediately drafted regulations, which were submitted by the ministry to the National Government for approval and promulgation, and ordered to be implemented. At the same time, I was also ordered to be appointed as the Acting Director-General of the Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau. I, with my humble talent, was repeatedly honored and dared not fail to work hard. However, I have been serving the postal service for 32 years and my mind and body are exhausted, so I have never released my desire to retire. Since the opening of the bureau on March 15, only five months have passed. The expansion of the bureaus has reached more than a hundred places. Various savings deposits have increased by several million yuan, and the results are not bad. The booklets and reports are sufficient to prove this. If military affairs are resolved and the overall situation is stabilized, then business prosperity can be guaranteed. In addition, I was ordered to improve the postal system and revise the postal districts, all of which are intended to unify authority, save national funds, and never have any prejudices. Those who do not know recognize it as seizing power for themselves. I do not know that I have exhausted all my efforts to explain clearly, see the new chapter implemented in the morning, and retreat in the evening. The resting place is there, how can I break my promise? Now that I have been away from the post office for two years, this labor unrest has even implicated me. The main reasons are nothing more than two points. One is that the reorganization of the labor union is suspected to be advocated by me, and the other is that the request for salaries and allowances is also suspected to be obstructed by me. The labor unions have this drastic action at the juncture of survival and interests. How does I, Shufan, advocate that the reorganization is under the control of the central government? You know it very well, and there is no need to elaborate. As for the salary issue, it is entirely a misunderstanding. What is even more strange is that the northern newspapers actually said that I, Shufan, withdrew 20 million yuan of postal funds and 2 million yuan of pension funds to contribute to the government as war expenses. The intention is even more heartbreaking. In short, various misunderstandings are all caused by the lack of sincerity and trust on weekdays and the lack of knowledge of the truth, which makes oneself a target of arrows. Thinking over and over again, it is better to give way to the virtuous today than to be blamed in the future. Furthermore, since July 10, I have suffered from a brain disease for two months and have not yet recovered. If I continue to support it reluctantly, both public and private affairs will not be cured. There is no other way. I express my sincerity and pray for your review and approval, and request that you forward it to request dismissal from the positions of Director of the Postal Department and Acting Director-General of the Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau, so that I can recuperate in time and avoid mistakes. I am infinitely grateful and cannot express my obedience. Sincerely present to the Minister and Vice Minister.

Telegram Ordering Prompt Issuance of Ship Rentals

Telegram from Commander-in-Chief Chiang to the Shipping Industry Association

The Shanghai Shipping Industry Association received a telegram from Commander-in-Chief Chiang yesterday, which read: The Shanghai Shipping Industry Association acknowledges your telegram. Regarding your request for the prompt issuance of ship rentals to various companies, I have telegraphed the rear manager and transportation departments to investigate and handle the case. Publication of British Ship Registry

33,000 Steamships and Sailing Ships Worldwide. The Zi Lin Bao reports that the 1930-31 annual ship registry of the British Lloyd's Ship Registry Committee has been published and arrived in Shanghai. According to the report, there are approximately 33,000 steam and fuel oil ships and sailing ships over 100 tons worldwide, and a total of 21,000 companies related to shipping. In the one-year period from June 1929 to June 1930, steam merchant ships increased by 148,176 tons, fuel oil merchant ships increased by 1,468,235 tons, and sailing ships decreased by 83,079 tons, for a total net increase of 1,533,332 tons. The previous year increased by only 1,119,653 tons. By country, Norway increased the most, followed by England, then France, and then the Netherlands. The United States, on the other hand, decreased compared to the previous year. As for the total tonnage, England still ranks first with a total of 23,100,000 tons, followed by the United States with 23,104,000 tons. Japan has jumped to third place with a total of 4,317,000 tons. However, the total tonnage of England accounted for 54% of the world's total in 1898, fell to 41.6% in 1914, and further fell to 29.9% this year.

[China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Emergency Loan]

Li Guojie Borrowed 55,000 Taels of Silver from the China Business Company

The financial situation of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is deteriorating, and employees are owed wages and coal supplies are often insufficient, resulting in the risk of work stoppages and suspension of navigation. Director Wang Boqun witnessed the difficulties and firmly urged the chairman of the company, Li Weihou, to find a way to raise funds to provide emergency relief. In order to take care of the overall situation, Li has borrowed 55,000 taels of silver from the China Business Company to maintain the status quo. The original text of the instructions of Director Wang on this matter is found and copied below.

Supervision Office of the Ministry of Communications of the National Government, Instructions to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (No. 114) To Li Guojie, Chairman of the Board of Directors of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Presenting a Document, Reporting on Complying with the Discussion of Raising Loans, Please Review and Record the Case, It is Known from the Presentation, Check that the current urgent needs of the bureau are waiting for the ship to sail. Since the General Management Office has run out of resources and cannot raise funds, the Chairman is still able to take care of the overall situation and has consulted with General Manager Cai and agreed with the China Business Company to borrow an additional 55,000 taels of silver to relieve the immediate crisis, which is commendable and should be approved for filing. As for the contract and other items, you should still consult with the general manager of the bureau to handle it. This order, September 1, 19th year of the Republic of China, Wang Boqun.

Existing River and Sea Vessels of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company

A reporter from the New Voice Society visited the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company yesterday and interviewed Mr. Shen Jiyun, Acting Head of the Shipping Department. According to him, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company currently has a total of 25 river and sea vessels. Those operating in the Yangtze River area include Jiangxin, Jiangshun, Jiangjing, Jiangyu, Jiangtian, Jiang'an, Jiangda, Jianghua, Kuaili, etc., a total of ten ships. Sea vessels include Xinming, Xinfeng, Guangli, Guangji, Haiyan, Xinjiangtian, Jianguo, Guangda, Yushun, Tunan, Tonghua, Jiahe, Xinchang, Shuntai, Gongping, etc., a total of fifteen ships. Currently, the Jiangjing vessel is under repair. Except for Jiangshun, Jiang'an, Xinchang, and Jianghua, all the ships are very old. Currently, in addition to handling military transport, the North Ocean shipping route has Xinming and Xinfeng ships operating, the South Ocean has Haiyan, Xinjiangtian, and Guangji ships operating, and the Yangtze River only has Jiangxin, and the upper Yangtze has Kuaili and Emei.

Special News from the Shipping Industry

The Number of Japanese Ships Increasing. In the first half of this year, a total of 3,938 ships entered Shanghai, totaling 9,771,400 tons, of which British ships accounted for 1,204, 2,841,100 tons, Japanese ships accounted for 1,195, 2,729,000 tons, and Chinese ships accounted for 875, 1,296,000 tons. Compared with last year, Japanese ships increased by 208, and exported ships from Japan had 1,246 ships, accounting for 2,866,000 tons, an increase of 239 ships compared with last year. The reason for the increase is that the Dalian Steamship Company and the Kawasaki Company have added new routes. Chinese ships, on the other hand, decreased by more than 300 ships compared with last year.

New Ship Opens. The Changchun Jiu, a new ship built by the Shanghai-Dalian Steamship Company, with a net tonnage of 4,000 tons, has joined the Shanghai-Dalian-Qingdao route. It has already left the factory and arrived in Shanghai yesterday. Its passenger capacity and speed are greater than those of the Fengtian Maru and Dalian Maru. It has arrived in Shanghai yesterday and will stay for four days for public viewing. It is scheduled to open the maiden voyage to Dalian on the 8th, and the 榊丸 ship will be changed to the new South China route, specializing in the ports of Shanghai, Hong Kong, and Guangzhou.

Continued Arrival of Hunan Refugees. Many Hunan refugees have come to Shanghai in recent days. Yesterday, the Japanese ship Xiangyang Maru and the British ships Gonghe, Pinghe, Poyang, and other ships arrived in Shen, and another large number of Hunan people arrived in Wuhan from Changsha by northern ships and transferred to Shanghai. They are all in a very embarrassing situation.

Rumors in Foreign Newspapers About the Silver Market

The Zi Lin Bao reports that regarding the silver market yesterday, there were unconfirmed rumors in this port that the Indian and Annam governments continued to sell, and a large amount of silver could be salvaged from the ship Egypt. It is said that at least one Chinese bank in this port received a message yesterday (2nd) that the Indian government is preparing to sell 40 million ounces of silver at a price slightly lower than London. If this message cannot be confirmed, people in the financial community have different views. Some said that it had just sold 15 million ounces to Hong Kong, and some expected it to continue to sell due to the decline of business. At the same time as this message was spread in the market, there was another message that the Annam government was selling 5 million old silver coins on the London market. In addition, there is a saying that the ship Egypt, which is currently salvaging gold, in addition to containing gold bars worth 1.6 million pounds of British gold, also contains 1.4 million ounces of silver bars. If the gold bars can be salvaged, the silver can also be shipped out at the same time.

The Naval Department is sending eight students to Japan to study naval torpedoes and naval logistics: He Xikun, Zeng Guoxi, Yao Yu, Ye Keyu, student Li Huiji, Meng Handing, Zhang Dacheng, and Chen Hong. Direct Wireless Telegraph Connection to Yingkou and Harbin

The Ministry of Communications' Wireless Telegraph Administration has recently seen the development of wireless telegraphy in the three eastern provinces. Radio stations are located in fourteen places: Liaoning, Harbin, Changchun, Jilin, Yanji, Suifenhe, Mishan, Qiqihar, Hailar, Ergun, Heihe, Manzhouli, Fujin, and Yingkou. There are also Sino-German radio stations and broadcasting stations. As for the Sino-American and Sino-French radio stations, they are still under construction. However, telegrams sent from Shanghai have traditionally been forwarded via Liaoning. Now, it is heard that the Shanghai Wireless Telegraph Bureau, in order to save time and expedite procedures, has agreed with the Harbin and Yingkou radio stations in Northeast China to establish a direct connection. This will be implemented soon.

Foreign Shipping Companies Unanimously Oppose Increased Wharfage Rates

Chamber of Commerce Submits Protest to Diplomatic Corps

The Jianghai Customs announced that wharfage rates would increase from the 16th of this month, with new regulations issued and collected. Subsequently, foreign shipping companies, feeling that the increased costs were too high to bear, jointly petitioned the International Chamber of Commerce to convene a meeting to discuss solutions. The meeting resulted in seeking opinions from various shipping companies. Yesterday, the companies submitted their written opinions. Nine companies, including Butterfield & Swire, Jardine Matheson, Nissin Kisen, and Osaka Shosen, unanimously expressed their opposition and refused to recognize the new regulations, adopting a strong stance. Therefore, the International Chamber of Commerce has submitted a protest to the diplomatic corps, requesting them to appeal to the National Government on their behalf.

Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Requests Prohibition of Re-Taxation by Chongqing Customs

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing yesterday, stating: "On the 2nd of this month, we received a letter from Wing On Textile Co., Ltd., stating that when their machine-made Jin Cheng, Jin Qian, Jia He, Da Zhong Hua, Bao Ding, and Hong Yu brand cotton yarn, cotton thread, and cloth are sold domestically, after paying the regular and additional taxes at the Jianghai Customs, other customs bureaus generally waive re-taxation. This was previously approved by the Ministry of Finance and communicated to all departments and customs bureaus. Recently, goods transported to Chongqing, Sichuan, are still being re-taxed. The company resubmitted this matter to the Ministry of Finance on July 2nd, with approval document No. 10703. We request that you telegraph General Liu in Sichuan and the Department of Finance to quickly investigate and order a halt to the re-taxation and ensure compliance with the regulations. We request your prompt notification."

"Currently, cotton yarn from various Chinese yarn factories being transported to Sichuan, such as Hong Kui Xing, Flying Boat, Race Horse, Golden Rooster, Sailboat, Cai Kui Xing, Cannon Tower, Three Sheep, Hong Fu, Ren Zhong, Red Lion Ball, Single Globe, etc., are exempt from re-taxation by local collection agencies. Only our company's goods have not been granted an exemption. We earnestly request you to telegraph the Chongqing General Chamber of Commerce, requesting them to ask the Chongqing Tax Bureau to handle our company's above-mentioned yarn and cloth transported to Sichuan in accordance with the regulations, exempting them from taxation and facilitating the national goods and helping merchants in difficulty."

"The Chamber of Commerce has investigated that the Jin Cheng, Jin Qian, Jia He, Da Zhong Hua, Bao Ding, and Hong Yu brand cotton yarn and cloth produced by the company were previously approved by your ministry for exemption from re-taxation. Furthermore, the Chongqing Tax Bureau failed to act in accordance with the regulations. The company also obtained approval from your ministry to telegraph General Liu and the Sichuan Department of Finance to halt the re-taxation. Now, according to the letter, the company's above-mentioned yarn and cloth transported to Sichuan have still not been granted an exemption. This violates national laws and obstructs the sales of national goods. We should telegraph your ministry for review and swiftly order compliance to maintain the industry, which would be in the public interest."

Recent Disaster Situation in Henan Province

The Jisheng Society Unable to Provide Relief

The China Jisheng Society has recently received successive telegrams from Chairman Li Shican of the Kaifeng Disaster Relief Association in Henan, stating that in the counties of Lanfeng, Yuxian, Tangyin, Mianchi, Gongxian, Luoyang, Shangqiu, Ningling, Linru, Chenliu, Kaocheng, Yanshi, and Zhecheng in Henan Province, some cities have been reduced to ruins due to military disasters and banditry; some have faced drought, locusts, and the suffering of children abandoned and on the verge of death; some have suffered from hailstorms, resulting in crop failures; and some have been engulfed in war, with houses reduced to ashes and lives worth less than grass. The suffering is difficult to describe. They hope that the authorities will take responsibility for rescue, and charitable organizations will show compassion, making a final effort to save those starving and drowning, with voices hoarse, strength exhausted, and tears dried up. They look to the heavens, awaiting relief for the parched land.

The association receives urgent disaster telegrams every day, coming like snowflakes, but they are unable to help. Furthermore, with soldiers and bandits everywhere and iron horses galloping across the land, they are unable to provide relief. After repeated consideration, they can only first send tens of thousands of bottles of disaster relief medicine, to be transferred by Mr. Yu Guisheng, director of the Tianjin Relief Office, to the Henan Disaster Relief Association in the disaster area for preliminary relief. Where can they find patriots to relieve the current suffering of the dying disaster victims?

Page 15

Local News Two

Suspicious Sudden Death of Daughter-in-Law of Constable Li Qingfu

Police Receive Anonymous Letter

Dispatch Detectives for Secret Investigation

Believe Entire Family is Suspect

Interrogation at the Court Yesterday

Li Qingfu, from Anhui, is of a mature age, and has served as a constable in the Public Works Department for thirteen years. He is currently stationed at the Gordon Road Police Station, so his family also lives at 666 Gordon Road. Li's wife, Chen, is forty-seven years old. Their eldest son, Yulong, is twenty-five years old, and their second son, Yukun (also known as Yufang), is twenty-one years old. Both work for the Public Omnibus Company, one as a ticket seller on bus number 220 and the other as a driver on bus number 22. Yulong married a woman surnamed Zhang from Anhui in March of the previous year. Zhang is one year older than Yulong. Not only are the couple's feelings harmonious, but they also get along very well with her parents-in-law, and the family is happy.

Sudden Death from Acute Sha (Heat Stroke) Unexpectedly, on the night of the 27th of last month, Zhang suddenly suffered from acute sha (heat stroke). Despite medical treatment, she died at 4 AM the next morning. Li Qingfu and Yulong purchased a coffin from Zhang Wansheng Coffin Shop on Datong Road in Zhabei. The body was placed in the coffin that afternoon and temporarily stored at the Yangzhou Guild Hall in Zhabei. The matter seemed to be settled.

Neighbors Become Suspicious Because of Zhang's sudden death, neighbors were unclear about the cause of her death and began to speculate. There was much discussion, with some saying she had been murdered by her family. Inspired by these rumors, someone wrote an anonymous letter and sent it to the Gordon Road Police Station and the Special District Court.

Entire Family Arrested Because of the rumors, the police chief believed that there must be some reason for the rumors. He dispatched detective Shao Jingfan for a secret investigation. Shao's investigation concluded that the entire Li family was indeed suspicious, so he arrested Li Qingfu, his wife, and their two sons.

Police's Argument Yesterday, they were brought to the Special District Court, where Judge Wu Tingqi opened the second courtroom for the trial. The police lawyer, Wang Yaotang, stated that the police had received an anonymous letter stating that Li Zhang had been murdered by her family. After investigation, they arrested the family. According to Li Qingfu's statement to the police, his daughter-in-law fell ill at 8:30 PM on the 27th and died at 4 AM the next morning. However, a female neighbor of Li claimed that she saw Li Zhang alive and well at 11 PM on the 27th. This is quite suspicious. He requested that the Zhabei government be contacted to move the coffin to the Forensic Examination Center on Ferren Road for examination. Li Qingfu and others are not currently being charged with any crime, but he requested permission to continue their detention until the body is examined, and then a decision will be made.

Bloodstains and Rope Marks According to the testimony of a worker from Zhang Wansheng Coffin Shop, on the morning of the 28th of last month, Li Qingfu came to the shop to buy a coffin and hired him to help with the placement of the body. He went with Wu Genfa and others and saw that the body was a female, and her inner clothing was already on. They only put on the outer clothing. However, at that time, blood was flowing from the deceased's mouth, and her arms showed reddish-blue marks, and her neck seemed to have rope marks.

Stern Scolding and Non-Stop Cursing According to Bao Wu, a female resident of 665 Gordon Road, next door to Li's house, around 5 or 6 PM on the 27th of last month, she was having dinner in the lane in front of the door. She saw the entire Li family having dinner together at the door. At that time, the deceased mixed cold rice with hot rice and was sternly scolded by her mother-in-law, Li Chen, who cursed her non-stop. She tried to mediate, but was ridiculed.

Funeral Procession Takes Small Roads After dinner, she still went to work the night shift at the yarn factory. When she returned home at 11 PM, she saw the deceased washing clothes at the tap in the lane. At that time, she heard people say that Li Chen had beaten the deceased. At 6 AM the next morning, she saw Li Chen carrying a bundle and going out. When asked where she was going, she said she was going to the countryside. Soon after, she learned that Li Zhang had died before dawn, and the funeral procession took place in the afternoon, not following the main road, but taking a small road through the wilderness to Zhabei. All of these circumstances are suspicious.

Defendants Request Bail Li Qingfu stated that he came home from work at 11 PM that evening. His wife told him that his daughter-in-law was suffering from acute sha (heat stroke). He went out to hire someone to perform sha scraping (a traditional Chinese medical treatment) on his daughter-in-law. Unexpectedly, she died at 4 AM the next morning. He reported this to the Gordon Road Police Station. The other Li Chen and her two sons all firmly stated that Zhang died of acute sha (heat stroke) and hired a lawyer to request that Li's father and sons be released on bail because the family had been arrested, leaving several small children unattended.

Returned to Custody Awaiting Further Interrogation The police lawyer opposed bail and stated that Li Yukun had applied for leave from the Public Omnibus Company the day after Zhang's death, and when Li Qingfu reported to the police station, he said that his brother had died, not mentioning that the deceased was his daughter-in-law, so he was clearly lying. Judge Wu then ordered the four defendants, men and women, to be separately detained for further verification.

From the Civil Detention Center:

Cai Yunhai Escapes

During the Wind and Rain Yesterday Morning

Cai Yunhai Escapes by Breaking a Window

Cai Yunhai, 25 years old from Guangdong, lives at 22 1/2 Tangshan Road. He used to run the Cai Chen Company at the intersection of Beijing Road and Museum Road, specializing in import and export business. He had entered into a contract with Guo Cunzhong, the owner of the Hua Feng Gold Shop on Xingbi Street in the French Concession, to deliver 500 dozen small pocket knives. After receiving the deposit, he failed to deliver the goods as scheduled, which led Guo to sue him in the Special District Court. He was detained by the court before he fulfilled the contract and delivered the goods in full. However, the deadline for the second batch of 400 dozen pocket knives was approaching, and Cai still failed to fulfill the contract. Guo once again filed a lawsuit. The court opened a trial the day before yesterday and ordered Cai Yunhai to post bail. Because he had no one to post bail, he was sent to the Civil Detention Center, where he was detained in a room on the third floor facing North Zhejiang Road. At 3 AM yesterday morning, during a heavy rain, Cai paced alone in the room, thinking of ways to escape. He saw that the bricks and mortar of the window on the wall were mostly eroded, so he secretly began to break down the damaged area, removing one of the iron bars protecting the window, and then escaped through the window. Although there was a slight noise at the time, it was drowned out by the sound of the wind and rain, so the guards in the center did not notice. It was not until dawn that they realized Cai had escaped. They reported it to Director Xie Fuzi, who reported it to the president of the court and notified the police stations to investigate.

Three More Robbers Apprehended in the Ten Thousand Yuan Robbery Case; Trial Begins

Investigation Reveals Liang Houbiao as the Robbery Leader

He Guoyan Claims His Wife and Nephew are Not Involved

The Zhejiang Local Bank sent staff to Shanghai to transport a large sum of banknotes. After arriving in Shanghai, they were robbed of 100,000 yuan by armed bandits while riding in rickshaws past the North Henan Road bridge. A few days ago, Detective You A'gen of the Old Gate Police Station solved the case, arresting eight men and women. After investigation by the Special District Court, one female was released due to lack of involvement. The remaining seven were detained separately. The day before yesterday, more gang members were apprehended and awaited trial. All these details have been reported in the newspapers. Yesterday morning, the police sent He Guo, He Xiangquan, and He Guo's wife, Xu Juhua, all from Shaoxing, to the court for trial. President Zhou Hanting opened the first court for the trial. First, the police lawyer Ru Baoyi stated the details of the arrest. According to Wang E, who was apprehended a few days ago, He Guo was an accomplice. Thus, Detective You, together with detectives from the Zhabei Police Station, went to 630 Pushan Road in the early morning and arrested He Guo first. At that time, He Xiangquan handed a piece of paper to Xu Juhua, who read it. It contained information about Liang Houbiao's arrest, so the two were also arrested. Chinese and foreign detectives reported the circumstances of the arrest. President Zhou then questioned He Guo, who confessed that he knew Liang Houbiao through Liang's brother. On the 27th of last month, Wang E came to his house and asked him to go to the North Railway Station to pick up a customer the next day. When Wang arrived, they took a rickshaw to the North Railway Station. When they arrived, four people, Zhu, Hu, Su Ma, etc., arrived in a car. The group went to a teahouse in the concession to drink tea. Later, they saw the train entering the station, and Zhu and the other three bought platform tickets and went to the front of the train. He and Wang E waited outside. A moment later, Zhu and others came out of the station and said that the customer had been picked up. The six of them boarded the original car, and Su, the driver, drove south. When they arrived at North Henan Road, they took out four pistols from their bags and gave him one. Because he was not good at using guns, he did not accept it. However, they threatened him, so he had to take the gun. The remaining three guns were divided among Zhu, Ma, and Hu. The three got out of the car. At that time, the victim was riding in a rickshaw. Ma suddenly snatched a bag. Zhu fired a shot. He stood next to the car. After getting the loot, they boarded the car and drove to a place in the French Concession. They let him get out of the car, saying that they would call him later. He went home. That evening, he was called to Liang Houbiao's house. Liang gave him 500 yuan, and another 500 yuan the next day. Liang had borrowed 200 yuan from him. He gave Liang another 200 yuan. He also returned 200 yuan for a past debt. He had 400 yuan left, which he deposited with a neighbor, Mr. Jia. After he was arrested yesterday, the detectives went to Jia's house to search for the loot, but the money had disappeared. The piece of paper was sent by Liang Houbiao's brother, telling him to flee quickly. His wife, Xu Juhua, and his nephew, He Xiangquan, had nothing to do with the case. He Guo also said that Liang Houbiao was the robbery leader and that they were just dividing the loot. Judge Zhou ordered the three defendants, men and women, to be detained separately and rescheduled the trial.

Kidnapping of a Boy After Failed Attempt to Open a Strongbox

Resorted to Kidnapping in Anger

The Zhou Sanhe Strongbox Shop at 149 Ayrlie Road is owned by Zhou Hankun from Jiangxi. Around 8:30 PM last night, four robbers speaking with a Shandong accent suddenly broke in. Each was carrying a pistol, with two wearing black silk short shirts, two wearing white shirts, and the remaining robbers wearing blue short shirts. After entering, three robbers broke into the inner room, and one stood guard outside the door. The robbers who entered the inner room ordered the shop assistant Jiang Hansheng to open the strongbox. However, the shop owner Zhou Hankun had not yet returned at this time, and the box could not be opened. The robbers tried every method but were unable to open it for about three-quarters of an hour. The robbers became impatient and abandoned the box. They grabbed the shop owner's six-year-old son, Fusheng, who was lying on the bed, and ran out of the door. Afterwards, the victim reported the incident to the Tilanqiao Police Station, requesting an investigation. The shop owner, Zhou Hankun, has been running the strongbox shop in Shanghai for more than ten years. It was originally located on Baoshan Road and then moved to Sikaizi Bridge for about two years. It moved to Ayrlie Road last year.

Ferry Operators Petition for Municipal Ferry to be Converted to Commercial Ferry

The Lan Ni Ferry in Pudong, one of the eight major ferries on the Huangpu River, has been providing ferry service to the Jiangtian Pier of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company on the opposite bank day and night for a long time. It originally started as a charitable ferry. Later, with the approval of the authorities, a fare of 3 cash per person was charged, later increased by 2 cash to 5 cash. Since the change of dynasties, the standard of living has gradually increased, and the fare has been increased repeatedly, from 1 copper coin to 2, 3, and then 4 copper coins. In recent years, the night business has been taken over by double-oared boats, each carrying seven passengers, with the fare increasing from 5 copper coins per person to 6, 7, and even 8 copper coins. However, ferry boats and rowboats, when the wind is calm and the waves are gentle, are relatively safe for passengers. In case of wind and rain, not only is the voyage extremely dangerous, but passengers also find it difficult to embark and disembark on both banks. Ferry operators such as Lu Shanshan, in order to ensure the safety of passengers, jointly petitioned the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities to convert to a steam ferry, but the application was not approved. Recently, the bureau tendered bids for steam ferries and planned to operate them as municipal ferries. The ferry operators, with their livelihoods at stake, unanimously decided to jointly petition the Municipal Government and the Bureau of Public Utilities to convert the proposed municipal steam ferry back to a commercial ferry. The petition was submitted yesterday and is transcribed below:

Petition to the Municipal Government, a petition for appeal. The people have long been engaged in the ferry business at the Lan Ni Ferry in Pudong. Recently, the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities has taken back the ferry for municipal operation, causing public anxiety. They jointly petitioned to continue to operate the ferry as a commercial ferry and convert it to a steam ferry to ensure the safety of passengers, but the application was not approved. The Lan Ni Ferry in Pudong is one of the eight major ferries. Since the beginning of the Qing Dynasty, it has been a charitable ferry. At the end of each year, it has been given rewards by the authorities to show their concern. Later, as the standard of living increased, the authorities approved the collection of fares to subsidize operations. The Municipal Bureau of Finance also collected donations and issued licenses to protect operations. Afterwards, the ferry business flourished. The people had petitioned the Bureau of Public Utilities to convert to a steam ferry in order to adapt to the trend. Under the governance of the party, the people's livelihood is the top priority. The people are 37 ferry owners at the Lan Ni Ferry, who have been able to make a living for generations. If the ferry is taken back for municipal operation, the people's livelihood will be completely cut off, and they will inevitably become starving corpses. If there is no way to provide relief, the consequences are unimaginable. They have no choice but to file an appeal, requesting the government to sympathize with the people's difficulties, revoke the instructions of the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities, and approve commercial operation to provide relief. They sincerely submit this urgent petition for review and compliance, which would be in the public interest. Respectfully submitted.

Petition to the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities, a petition. The Lan Ni Ferry in Pudong is one of the eight major ferries. Since the beginning of the Qing Dynasty, it has been a charitable ferry, so at the end of each year, it has been given rewards by the authorities to show their concern. Afterwards, as the ferry business flourished, the authorities approved the collection of fares to subsidize operations. In addition, licenses were issued to protect operations, all of which are on record. Furthermore, in view of the fact that steam ferries are safer than ferry boats, the people previously petitioned the Bureau to convert to a steam ferry, but the application was not approved. Recently, it was reported that the Bureau will convert the Lan Ni Ferry to a municipal steam ferry and build wharves and floating bridges to ensure the safety of passengers, showing the Bureau's dedication to construction. However, the 37 ferry owners have been able to make a living for generations, and their livelihoods will be completely cut off, causing public anxiety. Therefore, on August 10 of this year, a general meeting was convened, resolving to petition the Bureau to convert the above-mentioned municipal ferry to a commercial steam ferry for the benefit of the people's livelihood. In the midst of vigorous construction, this would embody the purpose of benefiting and nurturing the people. Please indicate whether this is feasible for implementation. Respectfully submitted.

Detective Team Uncovers Illegal Gun Trafficking Case

Involving Wang Kaitian, a Member of the Self-Defense Corps

Qi Haitian, the leader of the detective team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, recently received a tip from a Shaoxing informant, Shen A'kui, who stated that Zhou Xueshan and Xia Jiugen, who live in a straw shed in Caojiadu, are restless and involved in illegal gun trafficking. He requested that officers be dispatched to arrest them as soon as possible. After receiving the report, Qi Haitian immediately reported to the team leader, Lu Ying, and, under orders, led detectives Wu Kezhong, Wang Yueling, Yang Fuchen, etc., along with the informant, to report to the Sixth District Office and requested dispatch of the office's detectives. They went to the ferry near the Baocheng Yarn Factory to wait. At 2:30 PM, Zhou and Xia arrived, and they were arrested. When questioned about where they were hiding the guns, they confessed that they were hidden in a straw shed on Zhongxing Road. Then, they went to the Fourth District Office and, together with the police chief, went to straw shed No. 10 near the Yangzhou Guild Hall on Zhongxing Road and seized a revolver and 17 bullets. They also found a membership card of Wang Kaitian, a member of the second team of the Pengpu District Self-Defense Corps. Wang was not present at the time. His wife was taken to the corps for questioning. The corps leader stated that Wang was indeed a volunteer member of the corps but did not often come to the team. Wang had prepared the gun himself but had reported that the gun was damaged. At that time, a new one was not issued. Now that someone had reported that Wang was illegally possessing a gun and Wang was not at home, he guaranteed that Wang would be immediately arrested and detained by the detective team to clarify the truth. As for Wang's wife, because she was a woman, he requested that she not be taken into custody. At that time, Qi Haitian, with the corps' verification, released Wang's wife. However, regarding the gun seized in the case, the corps leader claimed that Wang had prepared it himself. Fearing that there were other circumstances, he took Shen, Zhou, and Xia, along with the seized guns, bullets, and membership card, back to the team to report to Team Leader Lu for review and asked him to order corps member Wang Kaitian to be brought to the station for questioning to clarify the truth. However, while the investigation was underway, the leader of the second team of the corps sent squad leader Li Guangfu, along with Wang Kaitian, to the station to await questioning. At that time, Team Leader Lu believed that the circumstances of whether Zhou and Xia, who had been arrested in the case, had conspired to frame someone were not yet clear and could not be judged. Since Wang had the corps' verification that he was a volunteer member, it did not seem appropriate to detain him rashly. He instructed the squad leader to bring Wang to the station for questioning the next day for further review. He questioned Zhou and Xia in detail. Zhou confessed that he was 28 years old, from Wujin, and lived at No. 40 Lao Baidu Ham North, Caojiadu. He worked as a mahogany worker. Xia confessed

Page 16

that he was 21 years old, from Anhui, and lived at No. 21 Guangfu Road, Caojiadu. Both confessed that a month ago, Shen A'kui from Shaoxing had asked them to buy a gun on his behalf. They asked someone surnamed Song, who then asked a stranger. Song said that he had a revolver with only a dozen bullets for sale for 32 yuan. Shen then arranged a time with them to meet at the ferry of the Baocheng Yarn Factory, and as a result, they were arrested and asked for investigation. After receiving the confession, Team Leader Lu believed that the case involved the illegal trafficking of arms, which violated criminal law, and immediately prepared a document to submit it to the Judicial Section for review.

Prisoner Chen Zhengming Executed by Firing Squad Yesterday

The Shanghai Garrison Headquarters issued a notice, Law No. 57, regarding the announcement. The commander of the 26th Regiment of the Fifth Division of the Army, Zhou Shida, reported that Chen Zhengming, a soldier who shot and killed Liu, the platoon leader of the First Company of the regiment, in Nanqiao Town, Fengxian, should be interrogated by the headquarters. The case has now been concluded. Chen Zhengming's premeditated act of shooting and killing an officer constitutes a crime under Article 284 of the Criminal Law of the Republic of China and should be sentenced to death. The prisoner Chen Zhengming will be identified and escorted to the execution ground to be executed by firing squad as a warning. This announcement is hereby issued for general knowledge. The person executed by firing squad is Chen Zhengming, 24 years old, from Shicheng, Jiangxi. September 3, 19th year of the Republic of China. [Signed] Hui, Commander in Chief

Men and Women Workers Burned to a Crisp

Man and Woman Die in Baolong Hospital

One Female Worker Also in Critical Condition

At the Shuanglun Toothbrush Factory on Xin Ma Road (i.e., Jiangyin Street) in Xiaoximen, a large number of alcohol tanks were stored. The afternoon before yesterday, a male worker surnamed Liu and two female workers, Liu and Gu, were working near the alcohol tanks when, somehow, the alcohol spilled. Flames erupted and smoke billowed. Neighbors, thinking it was a fire, immediately called the West District Fire Brigade. Fire engines and ambulances arrived at the scene and extinguished the fire. Later, they found two female workers and one male worker, all burned to a crisp. The Fire Brigade ambulance immediately took the workers to Shanghai Hospital. Due to the severity of their injuries, they were transferred to Baolong Hospital. By 11:00 AM yesterday, the male worker surnamed Liu had succumbed to his injuries. One of the female workers is also in critical condition. How tragic!

Son-in-Law Demands Wife from Father-in-Law

Xiao Maozi's Whereabouts Unknown

Tan Honglin, a Jiangbei native residing at No. 1, Lane 2, Nanlin Li, Zhabei, who currently drives a rickshaw for a foreigner, is 45 years old. The day before yesterday, he brought his son-in-law, Wu Wendian (28 years old), to a police station in the Fourth District, accusing him, "My daughter, Xiao Maozi, is now married to Wu. Since their marriage, Wu has repeatedly abused her. My daughter works in a silk factory, and Wu takes her wages to gamble. On August 13th, she received her wages, and my daughter's whereabouts became unknown. Now, Wu is demanding her from me and has ruined my business. Today, he asked me to a 'tea meeting'. When we reached Xinjiang Road, three people suddenly dragged me aside and, without explanation, cut me in the head several times with a knife. Please investigate." When questioned, Wu Wendian stated, "Xiao Maozi and I have been engaged for many years. I asked to marry her several times, but she refused. This year, we set the auspicious date of the nineteenth day of the first month. I hired a sedan to bring her from my father-in-law's house, but my father-in-law smashed the sedan. After repeated persuasion, he finally agreed to let me marry her on the twenty-third day of the first month. Not long after, my father-in-law taught his daughter to divorce me, but it was unsuccessful. Today, Xiao Maozi suddenly ran away. It must be my father-in-law's instigation. In the past, we had arguments, and we went to a police station in the Fourth District to appeal to the Municipal Police Bureau and even litigated in the District Court. The injury on my father-in-law's head was not inflicted by me," etc. Because the matter concerns harming a relative, he was instructed to appeal to the Municipal Police Bureau for investigation and verification.

Enticing Women and Forcing Them into Prostitution

Zhang Xia Shi Detained for a Year and a Half

Procuress Zhang Xia Shi abducted a sixteen-year-old girl, Zhang Xiaomei, and brought her to Shanghai this spring. Recently, she rented a house in the French Concession and forced Zhang Xiaomei to go out and solicit customers. The case was discovered by a French Concession detective, who brought Xia Shi and Xiaomei to the police station. Yesterday, they were brought to the French Court for investigation. The Western detective reported the situation. When questioned, Zhang Xiaomei stated, "My parents are both dead. In the spring of this year, Xia Shi abducted me to her home and lived with her until the second day of this month, when she ordered me to go out and solicit customers. When I refused, I was beaten. Now, I have been arrested, and I request release." Xia Shi stated, "I have always done small business. Last year, I met Xiaomei on the street and became acquainted with her. Because she was destitute, I took her in. She voluntarily became a prostitute, and I did not force her." Her remaining statements were evasive. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced Zhang Xia Shi to detention in a women's prison for one and a half years. Zhang Xiaomei was sent to the Jiliang Institute for arranged marriage.

Shameless Man and Woman Arrested Together

Zhang Pan Shi, the 49-year-old wife of Zhang Pu Long, residing at No. 9, Gan in Laobaidu, Pudong, was promiscuous. She was having an affair with Zhang Shi Quan. Because Zhang Pu Long was not home during the day and only returned late at night, she took advantage of this time for secret rendezvous and enjoyment. The night before last, Zhang Pu Long returned home around 10:00 PM. After opening the door, he did not expect Zhang Shi Quan to be hiding behind the door. As soon as Zhang Pu Long saw him, he asked what he was doing. Unexpectedly, Zhang Shi Quan grabbed Zhang Pu Long's throat, and Zhang Pan Shi began to beat him. However, Zhang Pu Long was strong and powerful. He grabbed Zhang Shi Quan and Zhang Pan Shi's wrists and shouted loudly. The patrol police arrived and brought them to the First Sub-bureau of the Third District. Yesterday, they were sent to the District Court for investigation.

Ningbo Fresh Fish Boat Robbed

The Ningbo fresh fish boat of Fei Jinmao recently loaded ice crabs and yellow croaker in Ningbo to be transported to Shanghai for sale. The afternoon before yesterday, when sailing in the sea area of Chuansha, about seventy to eighty miles outside the Wusong estuary, they suddenly encountered a red-headed pirate ship sailing towards them. When Fei's ship saw the red-headed ship sailing straight towards them, the crew was terrified, fearing a collision. They shouted to the other ship and tried to steer away. Unexpectedly, pirates swarmed out of the cabin of the other ship, stood on the deck, and, carrying long guns or broadswords, forced them to lower the sail and stop. The owner of Fei's ship, realizing they were pirates, instructed the crew to resist with all their might and pull up the sails to escape. The pirates saw this and opened fire, killing one crew member and wounding three. At this point, the crew panicked and ran into the cabin. The pirates swarmed aboard, attacking people indiscriminately, wounding another three or four crew members, and dragging the ship owner from his bed, demanding silver dollars. The ship owner said, "My fish boat has no large amount of silver dollars." After saying this, he went under the bed and handed over more than one hundred yuan to the pirates. The pirates did not believe him, saying, "Such a large boat only has this amount?" They beat the ship owner again. He begged on the ground, "If you find silver, do as you please." They searched all the crew but found nothing. At that moment, they heard the sound of a whistle approaching. The pirates stopped robbing. Before leaving, they kidnapped two crew members. After being taken to the pirate ship, the two crew members begged, and they were released. The two pirate ships fled towards the East Sea. Currently, Fei's ship is docked in Chongming. Yesterday, the ship owner prepared coffins for the two crew members who were killed and sent the injured to the hospital. He also reported the incident to the water police for investigation.

Confirmation of Sun Yizhi's Suicide

Detailed Information from Guangren Bureau

Family to Go to Ningbo to Claim Coffin

Sun Yizhi (erroneously written as "Yiding" yesterday), of No. 31, Chunde Li, Lanweiai Road, French Concession, a native of Nanjing, also known as Dinghong, left home on August 26th and went to Ningbo. On August 30th, he sent a letter from Ningbo to his sister, Sun Erbao, stating that he was committing suicide by drowning due to unemployment. The whereabouts of his body were unknown, as reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now confirmed that Sun Dinghong committed suicide by drowning in Ningbo. Around 12:00 PM yesterday, his sister, Sun Erbao, received a letter from the Guangren Bureau in Meixu, Ningbo, stating, "Our bureau today (the 1st) collected the body of a man from the water. He was about twenty years old, with Western-style hair. He was wearing a undershirt, an Indian silk small shirt, an Indian silk long shirt, a leather belt, Indian silk pants with half a pair of lining pants, silk socks, and elephant hide shoes. After an examination by the Yinxian County police, the coffin is temporarily kept in our bureau. The next day, a straw hat and an envelope were found on the Muddy Beach across the river. The envelope was addressed to the Sun Residence, No. 30, Tangjiawan, Chunde Li, French Concession. There was no paper inside the envelope. Has your family lost a man? Please reply immediately." The remains were collected on the spot by the local security officer Chen Hepai. After receiving the devastating news, Sun Erbao and his wife, Rong, were in inconsolable grief, a truly pitiful sight. After persuasion from relatives and neighbors, they were told to take care of the aftermath. Therefore, they asked relatives Hua Yongxing and Wang Jusheng, and his wife, Rong, to go to Shanghai-Ningbo today to identify the body and bury it.

Car Runs Over Boy

Yesterday morning at 6:50 AM, near the intersection of Dongbai Broadway and Maohai Road in the International Settlement, two Westerners were driving a rental car with license plate number 10276 from west to east at high speed. A six- or seven-year-old boy was standing by the roadside, looking around. When he saw the car approaching, he was terrified. The Westerners also panicked and could not avoid him due to their excessive speed, causing the car to knock the boy down. The wheels ran over his head, chest, and other parts, causing blood to gush out. He was barely breathing. The boy's family heard the noise, came out, and, together with Indian police, detained them at the Huishan Police Station and sent the boy to the hospital for treatment.

Zhang Lin Shi Dies Immediately After Getting Off Train

At the Shanghai South Station of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway, yesterday at 12:40 PM, the early express train from Hangzhou arrived at the station. In the third-class carriage of the train was a female passenger, Zhang Lin Shi, 47 years old, from Dajing, Taizhou. She was suffering from ascites. She had purchased a ticket from Jiaxing to transfer to Taizhou to return to her hometown. She was accompanied by her daughter, Chen Zhang Shi, and son-in-law, Chen Rongfa, who were also going to Taizhou. After the female passenger Zhang Lin Shi got off the train and was about to hire a rickshaw to go to the 16th Pier to transfer to a ship to Taizhou, she suddenly fell ill and died on the grassy area south of the station before leaving the railway boundary. The station police, Lei Tai, went to take care of the situation and reported it to the South Station Police Department, which in turn reported it to the District Court for investigation. Later, her son-in-law, Chen Rongfa, and daughter, Chen Zhang Shi, went to the court to request an exemption from the investigation and prepared a coffin for burial.

A male corpse was found on Huaizhen Road, Jiumu Di, yesterday. He was about forty years old and had a beard. What was strange was that he was completely naked. It is unknown how he died in this manner. Some informed sources said that this person had been ill for a long time and had also been in business before, but he had become destitute. Changing "Wood" to "Iron" on Injury Report

Judge Feng Reopens Debate

Li Zhu Shi, the owner of Demao Cigarette and Paper Store at the corner of North Sichuan Road and Peng Road, previously accused her uncle, Li Songtao, in the Special District Court of committing assault and causing bodily harm. Judge Feng Shide held a hearing and ordered a forensic examination to determine the extent of the injuries before issuing a verdict. On the 25th of last month, the debate was reopened. The lawyer representing the defendant, Li Songtao, first stated that the defendant was concerned that the plaintiff was faking injuries. Therefore, they paid close attention to the plaintiff's actions. On the evening of the 16th of last month, they heard the plaintiff's son, A Pei, whispering with his friend, Zhu Xingyi, about "sixty yuan for going abroad" and "iron weapon injuries." Later, they reviewed the injury report and found that it listed "iron weapon injuries." When the plaintiff was at the police station, they only claimed to have been hit on the head. Now, the injury report lists injuries not only on the head, arms, and legs, but also on the chest, back, and thighs. Therefore, the plaintiff's injuries are inconsistent. Unless the forensic examination was imprecise, the plaintiff must have been faking injuries afterward. After Judge Feng questioned and concluded the debate, he scheduled the verdict for the 25th of last month. However, the verdict was not announced by the due date. Judge Feng discovered that the "iron" character in "iron weapon injuries" on the injury report had originally been a "wood" character that had been altered. Considering that there was a major suspicion, he summoned the plaintiff and defendant and the forensic doctor to reopen the debate a few days ago. Judge Feng showed the injury report to the forensic doctor and asked who had altered the "iron" character. The forensic doctor testified that the original injury report listed "wood weapon injuries," and he did not know who had altered the character. The case has been investigated and is awaiting the verdict.

Cook Commits Suicide by Ingesting Smoke

Gao Jinlai, a native of Yancheng, 24 years old, was a cook at Siming Hospital. The day before yesterday, he had an argument with his sister at home over a trivial matter. He suddenly had a momentary impulse and committed suicide by ingesting raw smoke. When the poison took effect, his family discovered it and sent him to Renji Hospital for treatment. Due to the severe poisoning, treatment was ineffective, and he died around 2:00 PM that afternoon. The hospital notified the French police, who took the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall for examination. Yesterday, the deceased's father, Gao Hualiang, went to the police station to request an exemption from the examination. The police chief approved it. He then prepared clothes and a coffin for burial and transported the body back to his hometown for burial.

Small Note on the Collapse of Wall in Zhizhong Li

The land on the west side of Xixinqiao Street, Xizilaihuo Street, French Concession, belongs to Tongren Fuyuan Hall. City buildings and residential neighborhoods are currently under construction. The project is named Zhizhong Li. Construction has been accelerated in recent days, with delivery scheduled for the end of September. Due to continuous rain, about a dozen feet of brick wall suddenly collapsed at 10:00 AM yesterday. The sound was loud. Fortunately, the rain had stopped work, and no craftsmen were injured. It was a close call.

Wang Yuan and Others Distribute Flyers, Fined

After 10:00 AM the day before yesterday, many bookstore employees went to Fuzhou Road to inform the workers of various bookstores about the strike. The General Police Department's Political Department received a phone report from the Modern Bookstore at the location. They immediately dispatched Chinese and Western detectives Pan Lianbi and Pu Pu, and detective Li Haifeng, to stop them. When they arrived at the Modern Bookstore, the workers had already left the Modern Bookstore and gone to the Sishudian Joint Sales Department to carry out the same actions. By the time they arrived at the sales department, the group had left for other bookstores. They kept missing each other. Later, they encountered each other outside the Taidong Bookstore. They saw about a hundred workers doing the work of posting slogans and distributing flyers and trying to force the Taidong store workers to strike. The Chinese and Western detectives arrested four leaders, Wang Yuan from Wuxi, Cai Wuguan, Chen Yun from Hubei, and Wang Rong. The rest dispersed. The content of the distributed flyers was to demand higher wages, implement an eight-hour workday, and other preferential treatment. Yesterday, the police charged them in the Special District Court for violating Article 318 of the Criminal Law. During the trial, the police lawyer Li Zhishan added another charge in court, stating that the four defendants had used words and pictures to induce people to violate the law, violating Article 160 of the Criminal Law. After Presiding Judge Zhou questioned Wang and others individually, he sentenced each of them to a fine of thirty yuan. If they could not afford to pay, they were allowed to commute each two yuan to one day of imprisonment. The flyers were confiscated.

Private Gambling Clubs, Each Fined 100 Yuan

Wang Zimiao, No. 1, Fukang Li, Lafayette Road, and Xu Chunfu, No. 9, Dexiang Li, Lanweiai Road, privately set up gambling clubs and listening tubes to lure people to gamble, violating the prohibition. The French police detective learned of this and raided the locations the day before yesterday, confiscating gambling evidence, silver dollars, and other items. They were taken to the police station. Yesterday, they were brought to the French Court for investigation. The two defendants confessed that they had privately set up listening tubes to lure people to gamble. The judge sentenced each of the two defendants to a fine of one hundred yuan, to be confiscated.

Railway Department Promotes the Purchase and Use of Domestic Coal

Coal Production and Sales Association Sends Letter of Introduction

The China National Coal Production and Sales Association sent a letter to the Purchasing Committee of the Ministry of Railways in Nanjing yesterday, stating, "We have recently read in the newspaper that your committee is now under the Ministry's order to order 4,000 tons of domestic bituminous coal for the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway. It is evident that your committee has the enthusiasm to promote domestic goods by using domestic coal for national railways. China's coal mines produce the most and largest amounts of bituminous coal. Since the military uprising, transportation has been obstructed, preventing domestic coal from reaching its destination. According to the regulations of the Ministry of Railways, vehicles can be allocated by the Ministry as long as there is coal. The bituminous coal produced by the Boshan Coal Mine in Shandong is very suitable for the railway bureau. Our association is willing to introduce the coal produced by the mine to meet the needs of your committee. However, the Jiaoji Railway has only been open for a short time, and there is a shortage of vehicles. May your committee request the Ministry of Railways to order the Jiaoji Railway Bureau to allocate vehicles for the transport of this coal? Please reply to us."
